S. No. Query Reply
1 The total number of suicides reported within the
campus of each IIT for each year from 2014 to the
present year, 2024, inclusively. 0 (Zero)
2 The demographic details (such as age, gender, and
academic program) of the individuals involved in
each reported suicide within the campus for each year
from 2014 to 2024. Not Applicable
3 The reasons cited, if available, for each reported
suicide within the campus for each year from 2014 to
2024. Not applicable
4 The measures or initiatives, if any, undertaken by each
IIT to address mental health concerns and prevent
suicides within the campus since 2014. Some of the measures taken by IIT Jodhpur to
address mental health concerns and prevent
suicides are:
1. IIT-Jodhpur currently has two permanent
residential counsellors, one visiting counsellor,
and one residential Well-being Moderator.
They are highly qualified (One Doctorate in
Psychology and Two RCI Registered Clinical
Psychologists, and One with a Master’s in
Psychology). The Wellbeing Moderators reside
in the student hostels to provide first-hand
support in any mental health-related crisis.
Appointment of more counselling personnel is
considered from time to time as per the need.
The identity of the students is maintained as
confidential information.
2. The counselling team’s mobile numbers and
availability are informed to the students
through regular mailers posters in the hostels.
3. The students’ counselling team is trained on
a regular basis and they act as a bridge between
Counsellors and all students.
4. The Institute’s Primary Health Centre has a
visiting psychiatrist, who is also available on-
call in case of emergency.
5. In case of a psychiatric emergency, students
receive prompt medical attention and follow-
up.
6. Year-long mental health awareness programs
are conducted by the counselling team,
including during the Orientation for new
students and their parents, on important
occasions such as World Mental Health Day,

S. No. Query Reply
1 Tenure completion date of present
Director IIT Jodhpur As per the Order of the Ministry of Education, Govt. of India, “the
appointment shall be on contract for a period of five years w.e.f.
date of joining”. The Director, IIT Jodhpur joined on 10.12.2018,
therefore, the five years term was completed on 9.12.2023.
Subsequently, as per the Order of the Ministry of Education,
Govt. of India dated 28 November, 2023, the Director, IIT
Jodhpur, was allowed to hold the charge beyond 9th December,
2023 till the end of the Academic Year, i.e. 30th June, 2024 or till
such time as the regular incumbent takes over or till further
orders, whichever is earlier.

1 Details of the stipend structure for Ph.D.
scholars in NITs and IITs for the past 5
academic years. The fellowship is being disbursed as per the norms
& guidelines issued by MoE (MHRD)
2 Guidelines or directives issued by the Ministry
regarding the disbursal and management of
stipends to Ph.D. scholars in these institutions. A regular Ph.D. student admitted to the Institute will
be eligible for financial assistance as per the norms :
(a) A candidate having B.Tech./B.S. (four-year
program)/Master's degree with
GATE/NET(JRF)/NBHM (or equivalent) can have
financial assistance as per MHRD norms/or
equivalent applicable for non-science departments.
(b) The requirement of GATE is exempted for an
applicant with M.Tech or equivalent post-bachelor's
degree
(c) A student may be exempted from GATE as per
MHRD guidelines.
A Ph.D. student would be eligible for enhancement
in the scholarship after two years provided the
student has met qualifier requirement. The
enhanced fellowship will commence from the date
of completion of both the conditions. No arrears will
be provided due to delay in completing the qualifier
requirement.
The Teaching/Research Assistantship of a Ph.D.
student shall stop from the day of submission of the
Thesis.
3 Details of the fund transfer mechanism for
Ph.D. scholar stipends from the MHRD to
NITs and IITs for the past 5 academic years. No such information available
4 The timeline and frequency of fund transfers
for Ph.D. scholar stipends, including any
delays or discrepancies observed in the
disbursement process. The funds is being disbursed to eligible fellows on
monthly basis within 7 days of month end.
5 Procedures and protocols followed by the
MHRD in allocating funds specifically for
Ph.D. scholar stipends in NITs and IITs,
including any documentation or approvals
required. No such information available

The applicant has asked for clarification, Whereas
“information” does not include “clarification(s)” as
defined under section 2(f) of RTI Act, 2005. Definition of
information under section 2(f) of RTI Act, 2005:
“Information” means any material in any form, including
records, documents, memos, e-mails, opinions, advice,
press releases, circulars, orders, logbooks, contracts,
reports, papers, samples, models, data materials held in
any electronic form and information relating to any
private body which can be accessed by a public authority
under any other law for the time being in force.

2 The details of the ongoing development project
related to the clean room also the documents
related to it? Clean Room and its Service Building along with
Electronic Manufacturing Unit is being constructed in
Pocket B of IIT Jodhpur campus. The construction of
clean room and its service building is in progress with
the area of 1380 sq.m and its service building with the
area of 683 sq.m. The documents related to the said
project is already on CPPP portal and Institute website
3 To whom this project related to clean room is
given, also by whose authority it is passed and
alloted to the said person and what is the estimate
of the project? The tender for “Design, construction, supply,
Commissioning and Validation of Class-100, Class-1000,
Clas-10,000 and Clas-1,00.000 clean Rooms (AIoT Fab)
and its Service Building at Pocket B of IIT Jodhpur” was
published on CPP Portal and the Institute website with
the estimated cost of Rs. 44,16,75,663/-. The financial
bids had been opened with the approval of competent
authority and M/s IClean had found L-1. Hence, the
work has been awarded to M/s Integrated Cleanroom
Technologies Pvt. Ltd.
4 The details of the project of the clean room
including its estimate, total cost and by which
method it is alloted to the said person who is
conducting the work? The project of Cleanroom is EPC tender and has been
awarded to M/s Integrated Cleanroom Technologies
Pvt. Ltd. on the basis of lowest amount quoted by the
same. The quoted price of M/s Iclean is Rs.
44,03,18,000/-.
5 What is the proposed use of this clean room? The Clean Room will be used as a semiconductor
fabrication facility (1 micron level) for conducting R&D
and developing sensors & other IoT devices by faculty 7
students of IIT Jodhpur, with an aim to integrate them in
a system, catering to a variety of applications, as part of
AIoT Innovation Hub
6 Is there any lab related to animal research built on
campus, and if yes then the details of lab and its
use? The Shalihotra Animal House of IIT Jodhpur is a state-
of-the-art small animal research facility. This facility is
registered (Reg. No.2284/GO/ReBi/S/2024/CCSEA)
with the Committee for Control and Supervision of
Experiments on Animals (CCSEA), Ministry of Fisheries,
Animal Husbandry &amp; Dairying, Government of
India, New Delhi. The establishment is authorized to
conduct research for education purposes and breeding

S. No. Query Reply
1 Could you please provide information on
which IITs, NITs, and IIITs have
implemented the new National
Education Policy (NEP) 2020? IIT Jodhpur has implemented the New Education Policy (NEW)
2020.
2 I am interested in understanding the
entry and exit options available
specifically for M.Tech degrees as per
NEP 2020. The Institute has created exit policies for B.S., B.Tech., M.Tech.
and Ph.D. students. The B.S. students can exit with a B.Sc. degree
in Physics and Chemistry following the norms as specified by the
Senate. The M.Tech. and Ph.D. students can exit with Diploma
and M.S. by Research degree, respectively following the norms
as specified by the Senate.
For example, students entered in B.Tech. in Mechanical
Engineering can Exit with B.Sc. in Engineering Science, or B.Tech.
in Engineering Science, or B.Tech. in Mechanical Engineering
with a specialization, or B.Tech. in Mechanical Engineering and
Engineering Science. Institute is currently offering multiple
entries to the Ph.D. programmes. Other than the standalone
Ph.D./M.Tech.-Ph.D. programmes, one can convert to the
M.Tech.-Ph.D. programme even after completing 2-3 semesters
in M.Tech. programme if he/she meets the CGPA requirement.
As multiple exits, after completing 3 years in M.Tech.-Ph.D.
programme, a student can also convert into a part-time/external
Ph.D. student and avail an M.Tech degree if all conditions for
part-time/external conversion are satisfied.
The institute has also introduced the provision of registration
kept alive (RKA) for M.Tech. students. A student admitted to an
M.Tech programme who has completed the minimum credit
requirement of the first semester, can keep his studentship alive
while he is pursuing any professional activity, by opting for RKA
in subsequent semesters.
Bridge courses/certificate courses to facilitate multiple
entry/exit:
A modular programme with multiple exits in the form of
certificates, diploma and degree has been introduced. Further,
the Institute has recently introduced a transition path for
diploma students in Data Engineering and Cloud Computing to
pursue M.Tech. degree in Data Engineering.
3 Furthermore, I would like to inquire
about the procedure for direct admission
into the second year of the M.Tech
program in Artificial Intelligence at IIT
Patna. The query does not pertain to IIT Jodhpur

S. No. Query Reply
1 In Centralized Counseling for M. Tech./M. Arch./M. Plan: CCMT-2024 ,NITs & other
CFTIs admission, the eligibility requirement in qualifying degree is that the candidate
should have passed and secured 6.5 CGPA on 10 point scale or 60 % for
Gen/EWS/OBC and 6.0 CGPA on 10 point scale or 55 % for SC/ST candidates. But the
qualifying degree (B.Tech) issuing premier Institute/ Institutes of National importance
like IIT Jodhpur certifies that CGPA multiplied by a factor of 10 gives percentage , that
is CGPA 6.0 equal to 60% and CGPA 5.5 equal to 55%.
In CCMT 2024 brochure, it also states that only primary mode of evaluation (CGPA
or Percentage) mentioned in the qualifying degree certificate/mark sheet will be
considered while verifying eligibility. Conversion from CGPA to Percentage or vice
versa given by individual institute /university will not be allowed.
I Belong to Scheduled caste and my daughter graduated B.Tech from IIT Jodhpur with
5.8 CGPA. My daughter application is not considering for admission due to non
meeting of 6.0 CGPA for SC candidate as per CCMT2024 eligibility condition. But as
per norms of IIT Jodhpur CGPA conversion criteria my daughter percentage equal to
58 %, which is more than required 55% for sc candidate.
Is the CGPA conversion criteria set up by Premier Institutes like IITs not acceptable?
Also clarify that the quality of educational degrees /B.tech/CGPA obtained from IITs
is same as that of degrees / B.tech /CGPA obtained from colleges run by private
parties?
I request ministry of higher education to issue direction to all the higher
education institutes to accept the CGPA conversion criteria issued by Institutes of
National importance like IIT Jodhpur, which are established as per law in the country
for admitting in M.Tech courses.
Here I am submitting Page No 8 of CCMT 2024 brochure (complete brochure available
in CCMT 2024 web portal) and IIT Jodhpur CGPA conversion certificate for ready
reference. The query is not clear and
specific and does not pertain to
IIT Jodhpur. However, the
document regarding formula to
convert grade into percentage
prevailing at the Institute is
available in the public domain
and the same can be accessed

Transparency in the allocation and distribution
of monetary benefits is crucial for ensuring
accountability and fairness within public
institutions. The information sought in the RTI application are
voluminous in nature as the record is not available in the
requested format.
As per 7(9) of the RTI Act “an information shall ordinarily
be provided in the form in which it is sought unless it would
disproportionately divert the resources of the public
authority or would be detrimental to the safety or
preservation of the record in question.” Therefore, you are
requested to visit the Institute in office hours (09:00 to 17:30)
Hrs on working day with prior intimation to CPIO, IITJ.

unless the competent authority is satisfied that the larger public interest warrants the disclosure of such
As per section 8(1) (j) of RTI Act, 2005 "there shall be no obligation to give any citizen, information

interest, or which would cause unwarranted invasion of the privacy of the individual unless the central
public information officer or the State Public Officer or the appellate authority, as the case may be, is
satisfied that the larger public interest justifies the disclosure of such information"

Kindly refer to your RTI Application; the reply of RTI Application is given under:

Annexure ‘A’
Reply to Query No 5:-
Currently, various ministries and government bodies provide financial support and schemes aimed at encouraging and supporting
young entrepreneurs. Some of the prominent schemes include:
1. Startup India Initiative: Launched by the Government of India, this initiative offers various benefits such as tax
exemptions, easier compliance, and access to a dedicated fund for startups through Startup India Seed Fund Scheme
(SISFS). More information can be found on the Startup India website (https://www.startupindia.gov.in/)
2. Atal Innovation Mission (AIM): Under the aegis of NITI Aayog, AIM promotes a culture of innovation and
entrepreneurship. It offers grants and funding opportunities for startups and innovative projects through their Atal
Incubation Centers (AIC). Detailed information is available on the AIM website (https://aim.gov.in/)
3. MUDRA Loans: The MUDRA provides loans up to 10 lakh INR to non-corporate, non-farm small/micro enterprises. This
is particularly beneficial for young entrepreneurs looking to start or expand their ventures. Further details can be found on
the MUDRA website (https://www.mudra.org.in/).
4. Support from Department of Science and Technology (DST): DST offers various funding schemes under the National
Initiative for Developing and Harnessing Innovations (NIDHI), such as NIDHI Prayas, NIDHI EiR and NIDHI Seed
Support System which provides grants, fellowships and seed funding to startups. For more information, you may visit the
DST website (https://dst.gov.in/).
5. Schemes from the Ministry of MSME: The MSME Ministry offers numerous schemes for financial assistance, including
the Credit Guarantee Fund Trust for Micro and Small Enterprises (CGTMSE) and Prime Minister’s Employment
Generation Programme (PMEGP). Details can be accessed on the MSME website (https://msme.gov.in/).
6. Schemes from MeitY: The Ministry of Electronics and Information Technology (MeitY) has established the MeitY
Startup Hub to facilitate the growth of technology startups. Under its TIDE 2.0 scheme, financial and technical support is
provided to startups working in emerging technologies such as AI, IoT, cybersecurity, etc. More information about these
initiatives can be found on the MeitY Startup Hub website.
In addition to these government initiatives, IIT Jodhpur offers support through its IITJ Technology Innovation and Startup Center
(TISC) and iHub Drishti Foundation, which provides incubation, mentorship, and funding opportunities to its students, alumnus
and entrepreneurs.

• PG Diploma & Certification Programs:
Fees vary between ₹1-3 lakhs.
3 Course Validity:

there is a specific time period within which the course needs to be
completed). Each course has a specific time period for
completion:
• Executive M.Tech. Programs must be
completed within 2-3 years.
• PG Diploma & Certification Programs
have a validity of 1 year.
4 Equivalence to Offline Degrees:
Please confirm whether the degrees obtained through these online
programs are considered equivalent to the degrees obtained through
the traditional offline mode, as per UGC guidelines and any related
governing regulations. As per UGC guidelines, degrees obtained
through online programs are considered
equivalent to those earned through
traditional offline modes, provided the
courses are duly accredited by UGC or a
recognized regulatory body.
5 Accreditation and Recognition:
Are these online programs accredited by UGC or any other
recognized regulatory bodies?
Are these programs recognized by professional organizations and
employment sectors (both government and private) for job
opportunities? • IIT Jodhpur's programs are recognized
and aligned with the standards set by
UGC and AICTE.
• Online programs offered by IIT Jodhpur
are recognized by industries and
government sectors.

practicals or exams, which will be
conducted at designated centers.

discussion forums.

through webinars, virtual office hours,
and live Q&A sessions.
• Students also have access to digital
libraries and other academic resources.

students enrolled in online programs? IIT Jodhpur does not provide placement
support for its executive education students.

IIT Jodhpur is addressing dropout rates, particularly
among students from reserved categories. The institute
offers remedial classes, financial assistance, counseling
services, Peer Assistance Learning Program etc. IIT
Jodhpur also offers scholarships, tuition fee waivers to
SC/ST/PwD candidates for all the programmes and
income based waier in the UG programmes, and financial
assistance. Counseling services provide mental health
support and career guidance to students facing academic
or personal difficulties.

6 Retention and Support Programs for SC, ST, and OBC Students:
Does your institution offer any support services or retention programs (e.g.,
mentorship, counseling, financial aid) specifically designed for SC, ST, and OBC
students enrolled in UG, PG, and PhD programs? If yes, provide details.
What initiatives are currently in place, or planned, to address the challenges faced
by SC, ST, and OBC students that may lead to dropouts? The regular students belonging to SC, ST and PwD
categories are exempted from paying the tuition fee for
among the programs. Further, the tuition fee for UG
students is based on the family annual income. The
detailed fee structure may be referred for
more information at the below link:
http://academics.iitj.ac.in/?page_id=490
IIT Jodhpur provides counselling services to all its
students, free of any prejudice or discrimination.
Students can easily access individual counselling as well
as participate in group outreach activities for their
wellbeing.
However, if any instance of caste-based discrimination is
brought to light in the course of counselling, appropriate
referrals are made to the competent bodies like the
inclusivity cell who is responsible for addressing the
problems faced by the students belonging to SC/ST/OBC/
EWS/ LGBTQ and other minority communities in the
Institute. If the concerned student undergoes
psychological distress during this process, counselling
support is fully available through the professional
counsellors. Confidentiality and sensitivity are
maintained during such processes.

1 I seek information under the RTI Act, 2005, regarding the IIT Jodhpur is an autonomous Institute (Institute of National
Importance) governed by the provisions under the Institutes
of Technology (amendment) Act, 2012. Hence, IIT Jodhpur
has the authority to mandate participation in sports and other
curricular and extracurricular activities, including setting
attendance requirements. IIT Jodhpur incorporated sports
courses as per the requirements of curriculum as part of a
broader education philosophy. Further, the sports courses
offered by the institute are non-graded courses.

S. No. Query Reply of IIT Jodhpur
1 Subject:Query regarding eligibility criteris
for admission into 4 year Bsc Bed program.
I hope this message finds you well. My
name is Sontu Banerjee, and I am interested
in applying for the BSc BEd program at IIT
Jodhpur. I would like to inquire about the
eligibility conditions for admission to this
program.
Specifically, I wish to understand:
Eligibility regarding passing year for class
XII i.e if students having gap years(year of
passing Class XII and Taking admission
into the course) are allowed admission into
the course.
I would greatly appreciate your guidance on
the matter, along with any additional
details. To be eligible for the BSc-BEd (Secondary Stage) Programme at IIT Jodhpur, a
candidate should have cleared the latest National Common Entrance Test
(NCET) conducted in the year of admission to the programme, opting for the
subjects of Physics, Chemistry and Mathematics. The candidate also should have
a background of Physics, Chemistry and Mathematics in class XII.
Since shortlisting criteria can be set by the respective Institutes, in the admissions
cycle of 2024-2025, candidates who had given their class XII Board examination
before 2024 were eligible to apply with a gap certificate/affidavit. However,
going forward, this shortlisting criteria may be subject to change. Therefore
prospective applicants for the academic year 2025-2026 are advised to refer to
the website of the Integrated Teacher Education Programme
(https://iitj.ac.in/itep/) for further details and updated information on the
admission criteria.

Query 5 What was the exact ground on which basis each candidate was shortlisted for Yuva Sangam (phase-4) at IIT-
Reply The candidates for Yuva Sangam (Phase-4) at IIT-Jodhpur were shortlisted based on a detailed and multi-faceted
evaluation process, as outlined below:
Eligibility Criteria – Age and Application:
The program was open only to youth below the age of 30 years who had applied through the Yuva Sangam
portal. Applications outside these criteria were not considered.
Verification of Documentation:
Candidates were required to provide truthful and verifiable documentation. Any discrepancies or falsification of
information identified during the verification process resulted in immediate disqualification.
Gender Representation:
In adherence to Ministry directives, special priority was given to female candidates to ensure equitable gender
representation. This step was aimed at fostering inclusivity and diversity in the program.
District-Wise Representation:
Efforts were made to maintain balanced representation from various districts. To avoid disproportionate selection
from any single district, exceptions were made only for candidates demonstrating exceptional cultural skills or
contributions, which were deemed vital for representing the state of Rajasthan on a national platform.
Adherence to Ministry Guidelines:
The selection process was carried out in strict accordance with the guidelines established by the Ministry under
the Ek Bharat Shreshtha Bharat initiative. Judicious discretion was exercised by the designated authorities to
uphold the program’s objectives and maintain fairness throughout the selection process.
Engagement in Team Convocations:
Candidates were expected to actively and consistently participate in team convocations. Lack of regular
engagement indicated insufficient commitment, which was a critical factor in determining eligibility for the
program.
Competency Assessment:
Indian Institute of Technology Jodhpur

Query 6 Who all officers, students or candidates were involved for coordinating and implementation and making Phase-
Reply The successful coordination and implementation of Yuva Sangam (Phase-4) at IIT-Jodhpur involved
contributions from various officers, faculty members, and students, each of whom played a pivotal role. Their
roles and responsibilities are outlined below:
EBSB, Nodal Officer: The Nodal Officer oversaw the overall planning, execution, and coordination of the
program under the Ek Bharat Shreshtha Bharat (EBSB) initiative. The Nodal Officer ensured compliance with
the Ministry's guidelines and facilitated smooth collaboration among all stakeholders.
Faculty Advisor, Representative, Yuva Sangam IV: Representative, Yuva Sangam IV played a multifaceted
role in the program. As the Associate Dean of Student Affairs, Representative, oversaw student-related activities
and ensured alignment with institutional goals. Additionally, the Representative was responsible for managing
the financial aspects of the program, ensuring budgetary compliance and resource allocation for successful
execution. The representative also provided academic and cultural guidance to participants and contributed to
the strategic execution of the program.
Faculty Advisor, Representative, Yuva Sangam IV: Representative, Yuva Sangam IV accompanied the
students throughout the trip, providing constant support and guidance. Representative played an active role in
every aspect of the program, including logistics, coordination of activities, and ensuring the well-being and
engagement of the participants. Representative presence was vital in fostering a cohesive and productive
environment for the students.
Appointed Staff of Office of Student Affairs: The appointed staff managed administrative tasks, coordinated
logistics, and facilitated communication among participants and organizers.
Appointed Staff of Office of Student Affairs: The appointed staff supported operational aspects of the program,
including resource allocation and maintaining documentation for efficient program execution.
Student President, EBSB Group: Student President acted as a bridge between the participants and the
organizing team. Student President motivated participants, addressed their concerns, and contributed to the
seamless execution of activities.

S. No. Query Reply of IIT Jodhpur
1 How many FORM 31 has the institute filed from its introduction in As of now, no Form 31 has been filed by the Institute.
2 What measures are institutes taking for meeting compliance of form
31? What measures are institutes taking for meeting compliance of form In accordance with the Institute’sIPR policy, all research intended
for patent protection is notified to the Institute’s Intellectual Property
Management Group (IIPMG) and protected through the filing of a
patent application prior to any public disclosure.
3 What are the standard operating procedure or due process of institutes
for filing Form 31? There is no SOP for filing Form 31 at IIT Jodhpur. The filing of Form
31 is addressed on a case-by-case basis, as per the requirements of
each instance.
4 Does the institute have any internal guidelines or a policy document for
this? If yes, kindly share a copy The Institute does not have internal guidelines or a specific policy in
place for filing Form 31.
5 Does the institute collaborate with external legal advisors or consultants
for drafting and filing Form 31? IIT Jodhpur has empanelled IP law firms to provide legal
consultation and support as needed.
6 How has the institute created awareness among inventors about Form
31 since its introduction? Specifically, has the institute conducted any
workshops or training sessions on its usage? If yes, kindly provide the
details of such initiatives. The empanelled IP law firms of IIT Jodhpur communicate with
inventors regarding the requirements and provisions related to Form
31 prior to initiating the patent filing process. Additionally, the
provisions of Form 31 are discussed during one-on-one consultations
offered by the Institute’s IP Cell. However, no specific workshops or
training sessions have been conducted to raise awareness regarding
Form 31.
7 Does the institute believe that Form 31 requires any improvements? If
yes, kindly specify the areas where improvements are needed and
provide the reasons for the same. If no, please explain why the current
form is considered adequate. Under the RTI Act 2005 of India, only information that exists in
material form and is held or accessible by the public authority can be
provided. Opinions, advice, or views are not considered
"information" under Section 2(f) of the Act unless they are already
part of an official document or record. Hence, we are unable to
provide an opinion in response to this query.

diploma students to enroll in this BSc program. I kindly request clarification on why
diploma students are not being permitted to join now.
Due to this decision, Now my two years of study have been lost. If I wish to join the
course now, I would have to restart my degree journey from the direct second-year
admission process.
I kindly request your consideration to allow Diploma Students to join the program.
For the past month, I have been trying to reach out to the Futurense team regarding this
matter but have not received any responses by mail.
I sincerely hope you will not ignore this email and would appreciate your guidance on
how to proceed. Your prompt response would be greatly appreciated as I am eager to
